Jamison Brereton

93 (702)
Indra (except Indra and R╠еbhus 34)
Sukakс╣гa ─Ас╣Еgirasa
34 verses: g─Бyatr─л, arranged in trcas ╠е
This long hymn begins with an address to the rising sun (vs. 1), which is echoed in the first verse of the second tr╠еca (vs. 4 ), and near its end are two verses directed to Agni (vss. 25тАУ26). These paired addresses to other deities within an Indra hymn suggest the ritual context of a dawn soma sacrifice (though Dawn herself is not alluded to). Indeed, the soma offered to Indra is the dominant theme of the hymn, which becomes more insistent as the hymn progresses. Not surprisingly, mention of the aid and material wealth he will give in return for the soma is also not scanted.
Throughout the hymn Indra is especially celebrated as (best) Vr╠еtra-smiter: the simple epithet and its superlative form occur an astonishing nine times, even though the myth itself is treated only sparingly (vss. 2, 7, 14тАУ15).
As often, the tr╠еcas become more tightly organized toward the end of the hymn, with a partial refrain in verses 25тАУ27, and full-p─Бda refrains in 28тАУ30 and 31тАУ33, the latter being introduced (31a) by the same p─Бda that provides the refrain (31тАУ33c). There are also intra- and inter-tr╠еca verbal echoes in these later verses. The separate final verse (34) mentioning the R╠еbhus seems to have little or no connection to the rest of the hymn.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra

English translation:

тАЬYou rise, O sun, on (the sacrifice of Indra) the showerer (of blessings), the bountiful giver, famed for hiswealth, the benefactor of men.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Indra is one of the twelve ─Аdityas

Who hurls the bolt and works for man

English translation:

тАЬWho cleft the ninety-nine cities by the strength of his arm, and, slayeer of Vс╣Ыtra, smote Ahi.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ninety-ninecities: RV. 2.19.6;

Ahi = the cloud

Jamison Brereton

He who split the nine and ninety strongholds with his arm-strong (mace), and as Vr╠еtra-smiter smote the serpent,

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (flg. Grassmann) takes b─Бhv├▓jas─Б as an abstract tatpuruс╣гa (тАЬmit Armes St├дrkeтАЭ), but it has bahuvr─лhi accent and the other three occurrences are clearly bahuvr─лhis. I follow Oldenberg in so interpreting it and supplying v├бjra- as the head noun.

The Pp. analyses vс╣Ыtrah─Б╠Бvadh─лt as containing an unaccented avadh─лt. I prefer to read it with accented ├бvadh─лt, which allows the ca to conjoin two parallel relative clauses. Since in this interpretation the verse consists entirely of relative clauses, it must be dependent on either the preceding or following verse. Either would work, but the presence of an apparently resumptive s├б beginning 3a favors the latter.

Griffith

Him who with might of both his arms brake nine-and-ninety castles down,
Slew Vrtra and smote Ahi dead.

Geldner

Der die neunundneunzig Burgen gebrochen hat mit Armes St├дrke, und der Vritrat├╢ter erschlug den Drachen.

Grassmann

Er, der mit seiner Armeskraft die neunundneunzig Burgen brach, Als Vritrafeind die Schlang’ erschlug,

Jamison Brereton

O Vr╠еtra-smiterтАФwhatever today you have risen over, o Sun, all that is under your will, Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The two vocatives addressed to Indra, vс╣Ыtrahan (a) and indra (c), flank that to the sun (s┼лrya, b), with the first embedded in a 2nd ps. clause with S┼лrya as subject.

Only the unambiguous reference of vс╣Ыtrahan to Indra saves it from being applied to S┼лrya, but the effect is still somewhat unsettling.

The verb ud├бg─Бс╕е reprises ├║d тАж eс╣гi expressing the same action in vs. 1. In fact 1a #ud gh├йd abh├н is echoed by 4b #ud├бg─Б abh├н with the actual verb ag─Б╠Б(с╕е) substituting for the intervening particles of the former.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand the force of the v─Б in 5a, since this verse does not seem to me a logical alternative to vs. 4. Nor do I understand the ut├б-u beginning 5c, which should not be conjoining the dependent clause of ab with the main clause of c.

However KleinтАЩs discussion (I.450) of ut├б appears to be on the right track and probably can account not only for the ut├б but also for the v─Б, if the explanation is fleshed out a bit. It seems that the three verses in this tс╣Ыca, esp. the first two, are loosely parallel to each other, esp. in their third p─Бdas. Vss. 4 and 5 begin with a twop─Бda y├бd clause (though the two y├бd-s are functionally different), with the third-p─Бda main clause resuming with a t├бd that is asserted to be in IndraтАЩs domain: 4c s├бrvaс╣Г t├бd indra te v├б┼Ыe тАЬall that is under your willтАЭ and 5c (ut├б) t├бt saty├бm ├нt t├бva тАЬjust that (comes) true for youтАЭ тАФ with te matching t├бva and with s├бrvam and saty├бm, the referent and predicate respectively of the two t├бd-s, phonologically similar. Thus both the disjunctive v─Б and the conjunctive ut├б serve rhetorical purposes, marking parallel structures, even though those structures do not have parallel or contrastive content. The third verse (6) varies the structure a bit: instead of y├бd there are two y├йs in ab and instead of t├бd p─Бda c has t─Б╠Бn; moreover, c is not a nominal sentence attributing all to Indra but requires Indra himself to make a move (gachasi тАШyou goтАЩ).

But s├бrv─Бс╣Гs t─Б╠Бn indra тАж semi-duplicates 4c s├бrvaс╣Г t├бd indra тАж, and the same total control is implied.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand the force of the v─Б in 5a, since this verse does not seem to me a logical alternative to vs. 4. Nor do I understand the ut├б-u beginning 5c, which should not be conjoining the dependent clause of ab with the main clause of c.

However KleinтАЩs discussion (I.450) of ut├б appears to be on the right track and probably can account not only for the ut├б but also for the v─Б, if the explanation is fleshed out a bit. It seems that the three verses in this tс╣Ыca, esp. the first two, are loosely parallel to each other, esp. in their third p─Бdas. Thus both the disjunctive v─Б and the conjunctive ut├б serve rhetorical purposes, marking parallel structures, even though those structures do not have parallel or contrastive content. But s├бrv─Бс╣Гs t─Б╠Бn indra тАж semi-duplicates 4c s├бrvaс╣Г t├бd indra тАж, and the same total control is implied.

Jamison Brereton Notes
04-06 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand the force of the v─Б in 5a, since this verse does not seem to me a logical alternative to vs. 4. Nor do I understand the ut├б-u beginning 5c, which should not be conjoining the dependent clause of ab with the main clause of c.

However KleinтАЩs discussion (I.450) of ut├б appears to be on the right track and probably can account not only for the ut├б but also for the v─Б, if the explanation is fleshed out a bit. It seems that the three verses in this tс╣Ыca, esp. the first two, are loosely parallel to each other, esp. in their third p─Бdas. Vss. 4 and 5 begin with a twop─Бda y├бd clause (though the two y├бd-s are functionally different), with the third-p─Бda main clause resuming with a t├бd that is asserted to be in IndraтАЩs domain: 4c s├бrvaс╣Г t├бd indra te v├б┼Ыe тАЬall that is under your willтАЭ and 5c (ut├б) t├бt saty├бm ├нt t├бva тАЬjust that (comes) true for youтАЭ тАФ with te matching t├бva and with s├бrvam and saty├бm, the referent and predicate respectively of the two t├бd-s, phonologically similar. Thus both the disjunctive v─Б and the conjunctive ut├б serve rhetorical purposes, marking parallel structures, even though those structures do not have parallel or contrastive content. The third verse (6) varies the structure a bit: instead of y├бd there are two y├йs in ab and instead of t├бd p─Бda c has t─Б╠Бn; moreover, c is not a nominal sentence attributing all to Indra but requires Indra himself to make a move (gachasi тАШyou goтАЩ).

But s├бrv─Бс╣Гs t─Б╠Бn indra тАж semi-duplicates 4c s├бrvaс╣Г t├бd indra тАж, and the same total control is implied.

English translation:

тАЬIndra was created for giving; he, the most mighty was set over the exhilarating Soma; he, the gloriousone the lord of praise, is worthy of the Soma.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Made = bale; Indra was created: by Praj─Бpati at the time ofcreation

Jamison Brereton

Indra is the one made for giving. Strongest is he when ensconced in exhilaration;
brilliant is he who, deserving of soma, receives the (invitatory) call.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Unusual syntactically, in having three non-initial s├б’s; what special effect is being aimed at is not entirely clear.

Griffith

Indra was made for giving, set, most mighty, o’er the joyous draught.
Bright, meet for Soma, famed in song.

Geldner

Dieser Indra ist zum Schenken geschaffen, der St├дrkste ist f├╝r den Rausch bestimmt; er ist der Glanzvolle, Ber├╝hmte, Somaw├╝rdige.

Grassmann

Zur Gab’ ist Indra angethan, der st├дrkste ist in Rausch versetzt, Er, licht und laut, dem Soma hold.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe mighty (Indra), unassailed by his foes, hastens to confer wealth on his worshippers– renderedkeen by their praises as a weapon, full of strength and invincible.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъс╣гvaс╕е = ugraс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Like a mace equipped with a hymn, powerful, not to be budged, he has waxed high, not to be laid low.

Griffith

By song as ’twere, the powerful bolt which none may parry was prepared
Lofty, invincible he grew.

Geldner

Wie seine Keule durch die Lobrede instand gesetzt, ist er kr├дftig, unentwegt, ├╝bergro├Я, un├╝berwindlich herangewachsen.

Grassmann

Durch Sang bereitet wie der Blitz, voll Kraft und unersch├╝tterlich, Erstand der hohe, unbesiegt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, worthy of our praise, do you, hymned by us, make our path plural in even in the midst of difficulties,(hear us), Maghavan, if you love us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Even in difficult going, make easy passage for us when you are hymned, o Indra who yearn for hymns,
if you will so desire, bounteous oneтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The contrastive dur-g├б- тАж su-g├б- effect is not easily captured in English because тАЬeasy goingтАЭ is blocked by the English idiom.

In c ca in the sense тАШifтАЩ conditions the accent on the verb v├б┼Ыaс╕е. See Klein (DGRV I.238-56, esp. 250-51, on subordinating ca.

Griffith

Indra, Song-lover, lauded, make even in the wilds fair ways for us,
Whenever, Maghavan, thou wilt.

Geldner

Auch auf unwegsamer Strecke schaff uns gepriesen guten Weg, du lobbegehrender Indra, wenn du, Gabenreicher, es willst!

Grassmann

Im Unwegsamen schaff uns Bahn, liedholder Indra, hochgelobt, Sobald du m├дchtiger es willst,

English translation:

тАЬYou whose command and rightful empire neither god nor irresistible hero can harm.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Rightful empire:svar─Бjya = svargasv─Бmitva

Jamison Brereton

You whose aim, whose sovereignty they never confoundтАФ
neither god, nor the exalted folk.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The implicitly conjoined nouns ─Бd├н┼Ы- (тАШaim, intentionтАЩ) and svar─Б╠Бjya- (тАШsovereignty, self-ruleтАЩ) do not seem to me to form a natural class. It is possible that the rendering of the former should be adjusted, to harmonize with the finite verb in 15b. The Pp. analyzes that verb as simply adiс╣гс╣нa without preverb, but in its sandhi situation it could also reflect ─Б╠Б-(a)diс╣гс╣нa, with the same lexeme as here. Even so, the middle voice of that verb would separate its semantics from the standard active idiom ─Б╠БтИЪdi┼Ы тАШpoint to, aim atтАЩ.

Thou whose commandment and behest of sovran sway none disregards,
Neither audacious man nor God.

Grassmann

Du, dessen Plan und Willensmacht niemand zu hemmen je vermag, Nicht Gott, nicht Mensch, der vorw├дrts st├╝rmt.

Jamison Brereton

And after that he became a covering for me: the Vr╠еtra-smiter displayed his masculine natureтАФ
he for whom no rival has been born, he who cannot be laid low.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Judging from GeldnerтАЩs tr. of the first p─Бda, тАЬDavor sei mir Bewahrung,тАЭ he takes ─Б╠Бt as an ablative pronoun referring to ├бmaс╕е in 14c (his тАЬPanik,тАЭ my тАЬonslaughtтАЭ), but as far as I can tell, ─Б╠Бt is elsewhere only adverbial, as opposed to the fuller pronominal form asm─Б╠Бt. I also question his modal, indeed imperatival interpretation of bhuvat in this preterital context; thematic forms belonging originally to the root aorist stem (├б)bh┼л- can be either subjunctive or a secondarily thematicized injunctive. See Hoffmann 1967 passim, esp. 214-15.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬO you bearing many names and praised by many, when you are present at our various Soma-libations,may we be endowed with a kine-desiring mind.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May we be endowed: maywe obtain kine;

Gavyay─Б = with adesire for milk; come with this mind, with this desire for milk, whenyou are present at our Soma-offerings

Jamison Brereton

(I inspired you, Indra,) with this visionary thought and with desire for cattleтАФo you of many names, praised by manyтАФ
so that you appeared at every soma-pressing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verse is syntactically incomplete, consisting of an instrumental phrase (p─Бda a), a vocative phrase (p─Бda b), and a subordinate clause with a verb in the imperfect (─Б╠Б-abhavaс╕е, so Pp.) or possibly injunctive (─Б╠Бbhavaс╕е). In order to provide a main clause for the y├бd clause, Geldner supplies тАЬgeschah esтАЭ (тАЬit happenedтАЭ). I prefer to borrow the verb of the preceding verse, ─Б╠Б┼Ыuс╣гe, though transposed into a past tense.

Griffith

To come, Much-lauded! Many-named with this same thought that longs for milk,
Whene’er the Soma juice is shed.

Geldner

Durch diese Dichtung und in dem Wunsch nach Rindern geschah es, du Vielarmiger, Vielgepriesener, da├Я du bei jedem Soma erschienen bist.

Grassmann

Durch diese Bitte voll Begier, vielnam’ger, vielgepriesener, So oft beim Soma du erschienst.

English translation:

тАЬShowerer (of blessings), with what coming of yours do you gladden us, with what coming bring you(wealth) to your worshippers?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Coming) with what help for us do you reach exhilaration, bull? With what (help) for the pressers? Bring it here!

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse presents both a conceptual difficulty (in ab) and a syntactic one (in c). As for the first, Indra should not be reaching exhilaration though his help for us, but rather through our soma. Geldner sidesteps the difficulty by simply reinterpreting the lexeme abh├н pr├б тИЪmand as meaning тАШdraw nearтАЩ (тАЬziehst du her zu unsтАЭ) without comment, but this relatively common collocation elsewhere always has the meaning expected of тИЪmad / mand, a meaning that abh─л╠БтАж mandas─Бn├бс╕е in 21ab would reinforce. In order to avoid the conceptually unlikely тАЬby what help for us do you become exhilarated?тАЭ I have supplied тАЬcomingтАЭ with the kay─Б╠БтАж ┼лty─Б╠Бphrase - re-establishing the usual balance between what Indra bestows on his worshippers and the soma they offer him in return.

As for the syntactic problem, imperatives (here bhara) should not appear in interrogative sentences, and p─Бda c begins with interrogative k├бy─Б. Geldner suggests that the 2nd ps. imperative here is used in analogy to the 1st ps.; in other words, since the subjunctive is perfectly at home in interrogative clauses and the 1st ps. subjunctive ultimately comes to serve as the 1st ps. imperative, its use in interrogative clauses could serve as a model for the introduction of 2nd ps. imperatives in such clauses. But I doubt that the 1st ps. subjunctive had been reinterpreted as an imperative at this era, since the full subjunctive paradigm in all three persons was still very much alive, and in fact Oldenberg comments that he does not know of other examples in the older language.

To avoid the syntactic clash I assume that k├бy─Б stotс╣Ы╠Бbhyaс╕е, parallel to k├бy─Б тАж na ┼лty─Б╠Бin a, ends the sentence, and ─Б╠Бbhara constitutes a new, abrupt imperatival clause.

Oldenberg cites a similar solution, though taking stotс╣Ы╠Бbhyaс╕е with the imperative not the kay─Б╠Бclause, found in GrassmannтАЩs tr., also in Caland/HenryтАЩs, which he dismisses as тАЬk├╝nstliches Ueberspringen der Schwierigkeit.тАЭ This hardly seems fair, since it does in fact avoid the difficulty, and seems no more artificial than many interpretations of syntactically awkward passages. As for my division into clauses as opposed to that of Grassmann and Cal/Hen, although stotс╣Ы╠Бbhya ─Б╠Бbhara is found several times elsewhere as a syntagm (V.6.1 [and reps.], nearby VIII.77.8), p─Бda-final ─Б╠Бbhara is extraordinarily common and could easily be construed independently, especially since stotс╣Ы╠Бbhyaс╕е would naturally pair with naс╕е in these parallel expressions.

Griffith

O Hero, with that aid dost thou delight us, with what succour bring

Mit welcher Gunst ziehst du her zu uns, du Bulle, mit welcher willst du den S├дngern etwas bringen?

Mit welcher H├╝lfe willst du uns erfreuen, o du starker Held? Mit welcher? bring den S├дngern sie.

тАЬRejoicing (in our oblations), bring us wealth a thousandfold; remember that you are the giver to yourvotary.тАЭ

Become a provider to the pious man.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese Soma-libations with their wives proceed (to Indra) longing to be drunk; the stale Soma, plural asingto the taste, goes to the waters.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Y─Бska, Nirukta 5.18: patn─лvantaс╕е = with their wives or protectresses: anallusion to the two kinds of water, the vasat─лvaryaс╕е and the ekadhan─Бс╕е, used in the Soma offerings (AitareyaBr─Бhmaс╣Зa 2.20). At the time of the avabhс╣Ыtha, or concluding ceremonies of purification, the с╣Ыj─лс╣гa or staleSoma is thrown into the waters. nicumpunaс╣Зaс╕е = n─лcam─Бnena pс╣Ыс╣З─Бti

Jamison Brereton

These pressed drinks here, accompanied by their wives [=waters], go eagerly in pursuit.
Regularly coming, ever filling [?] is (the wave) of the waters.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Though v─лt├бye is translated as if it were a loc. (тАЬin pursuitтАЭ), it is of course a dative, and тАЬIndraтАЭ or тАЬyouтАЭ should probably be supplied as object of the infinitive. The тАЬwivesтАЭ of the pressed drinks are, acdg. to S─Бyaс╣Зa. and followed by Geldner (and me), the waters; in this soma context cows, standing for cowsтАЩ milk, are also possible, though the occurrence of waters in c supports S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs suggestion.

P─Бda c is difficult, primarily because of the uncertain nicumpun├бс╕е but also because of the genitive case of ap─Б╠Бm. To take the latter issue first, Geldner assumes the referent of the nominative phrase is Indra, as тАЬder тАж Besucher der Gew├дsserтАЭ (ap─Б╠Бс╣Г j├бgmiс╕е). Since j├бgmi- in the singular is ordinarily used of Indra, this identification makes sense, but j├бgmi-, like other nominals of the same formation, always takes verbal rection, and the goal is expressed in the acc. (─Б╠Бhavam II.33.11, nс╣Ыс╣г─Бdanam VII.20.1) or loc. (vid├бtheс╣гu I.89.7) - not the gen., as GeldnerтАЩs tr. requires. For the baffling nicumpuс╣З├б (and its mantra variants -cuс╣Еkun├б- and -caс╣Еkuna) see EWA s.v. with lit. Mayrhofer cites there an etymological suggestion of WerbaтАЩs based on a proposed MIA form, meaning тАШalways fillingтАЩ. Though there is, of course, no certainty here, I have adopted this suggestion for want of anything better, though тАШgushing downwardтАЩ or GeldnerтАЩs тАШsprudelnde (?)тАЩ vel sim. would also work; consider also OldenbergтАЩs тАЬvielleicht ein dem Wasser innewohnender lustrierender Genius.тАЭ In any case, meanings in this sphere do not fit Indra terribly well (as GeldnerтАЩs тАЬ?тАЭ in part indicates), and, coupled with the problem of the case form of ap─Б╠Бm, this suggests that a different referent be sought for the nominatives in this p─Бda. I tentatively suggest supplying ┼лrm├н- тАШwaveтАЩ, regularly found with ap─Б╠Бm, esp. in soma contexts.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe sacrificing priests, invigorating (Indra) by their offerings at the sacrifice, have by their mightdismissed him to the avabhс╣Ыtha.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The desirable [/offered] libations, strengthening Indra at the ceremony, have surged
to his down-stroke with their power.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first word of the verse, iс╣гс╣н─Б╠Бс╕е, can belong either to тИЪiс╣г тАШdesireтАЩ (or the other тИЪiс╣г тАШsendтАЩ) or тИЪyaj тАШsacrifice, offerтАЩ and should be read as a pun. With Geldner the published translation takes ├нndram as governed by vс╣Ыdh─Б╠Бsaс╕е (тАЬstrengthening IndraтАЭ / тАЬden Indra тАж st├дrkendтАЭ). I took it so because asс╣Ыkс╣гata has a clear acc. goal in c and does not need another one. However, I am increasingly uncomfortable with this interpretation, since vс╣Ыdh├б- otherwise takes the genitive (see nearby VIII.98.5 sunvat├│ vс╣Ыdh├бс╕е and 6 m├бnor vс╣Ыdh├бс╕е), and I would now take ├нndram as another goal with asс╣Ыkс╣гata, hence тАЬтАж libations, strengthening at the ceremony, have surged to Indra, to his downstrokeтАЭ).

The word avabhс╣Ыth├б- in c is found only here in the RV. In classical ┼Ыrauta ritual the avabhс╣Ыtha is the тАЬfinal bathтАЭ taken by the sacrificer and his wife at the conclusion of the ritual, and it is interpreted thus here by Grassmann, and, although Geldner doubts that it is the final bath, he still takes it as a тАЬReinungsbad.тАЭ I am dubious for a number of reasons, not least that no one should be bathing in libations (h├│tr─Бс╕е) and that the participants in the final bath of later ritual are not gods (as Indra would be here) but mortals. Instead I think that the verbal lexeme ├бva тИЪbhс╣Ы, lit. тАШbear downтАЩ, provides the interpretational context for this noun. In the RV verbal forms of this lexeme sometimes take a weapon in the acc., depicting IndraтАЩs bringing this weapon down on his opponent (e.g., I.32.9 ├нndro asy─Б ├бva v├бdhar jabh─Бra тАЬIndra brought his weapon down upon herтАЭ; also v├бjram X.113.5), or, with an accusative of the opponent or one of his body parts, of Indra bringing down his enemy (e.g., II.20.6 ├бva тАж ┼Ы├нro bharad d─Бs├бsaya тАЬhe brought down the head of the D─БsaтАЭ). Here I think it refers concretely to IndraтАЩs тАЬdown-stroke,тАЭ which is strengthened by the soma offered to him.

English translation:

тАЬResplendent (Agni), these Soma-libations are effused for you, the clipped grass is spread; bring Indrahere for his worshippers.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For you have these soma drinks here been pressed and the ritual grass strewn, o you of radiant goods [=Agni].
Convey Indra hither for the praisersтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verse begins with a 2nd ps. pronoun t├║bhyam, and the content of what follows, until the end of b, seems entirely consonant with Indra as the 2nd ps. referent.

However, the vocative closing b, vibh─Бvaso, otherwise used only of Agni, and the fact that Indra is the 3rd ps. object of the imperative ─Б╠Бvaha in c, whose subject should be Agni, call the interpretation of the earlier part of the verse into question. Yet it is next to impossible, in my view, that the announcing of the soma drinks in a is made to anyone but Indra, and so we must reckon with a half verse that changed horses in midstream, as it were, without any poetic benefit accruing.

English translation:

тАЬMay he give strength and his brilliant heaven and precious things to you his worshipper, and to hispraising priests; worship Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Agni,) as you diffuse your skill through the luminous realms and distribute treasures to the pious man.
(All of you,) recite to Indra for the praisers.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand GeldnerтАЩs assertion (n. to 26a), that this verse only makes sense if Agni is the speaker, a view shared by Oldenberg I certainly agree that Agni is the subject: I take 26ab as dependent on 25c, where Agni is the 2nd ps. addressee, and take the participle d├бdhat of b with the objects found in both a and b, with slightly different senses (тАШdiffuseтАЩ in a, тАШdistributeтАЩ in b, both with preverb v├н).

The VP тАЬdiffuse your skillтАЭ refers to AgniтАЩs sending his light upward and outward; the тАЬskillтАЭ in question is preumably his ritual skill, his ability to conduct the oblations to heaven.

The 2nd pl. impv. in c must be addressed to the whole set of ritual participants.

Geldner insists (n. to 26c) that stotс╣Ы╠Бbhyaс╕е must be read with p─Бda b, parallel to d─Б┼Ы├║с╣гe тАЬdie Kleinode verteile f├╝r den Opfernden, f├╝r die S├дnger,тАЭ but the rigid parallelism of the c p─Бdas in this tс╣Ыca suggests rather that it belongs with its p─Бda. Presumably the full set of participants are chanting on behalf of the subset of тАЬpraisers.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, the first p─Бda of the first verse of this tс╣Ыca provides its refrain, a slightly odd effect. Only in 31 is the refrain syntactically integrated into the verse. There are also echoes of previous verses: ┼Ыatakrato, which ends 27b and 28b, appears as nom. ┼Ыat├бkratuс╕е at the end of 32b. The voc. vс╣Ыtrahantama of 30a is echoed by nom. vс╣Ыtrah├бntamaс╕е in 32a and voc. vс╣Ыtrahan in the same metrical position in 33a. The end of this hymn is very tightly constructed.

To our libation with thy Steeds.

Komm mit den Falben zu unserem Soma, du Herr der R├дusche, mit den Falben zu unserem Soma!

O komme mit den F├╝chsen her, zum Soma, Herr der Tr├дnke du, Mit F├╝chsen komm zu unserm Trank.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, the first p─Бda of the first verse of this tс╣Ыca provides its refrain, a slightly odd effect. Only in 31 is the refrain syntactically integrated into the verse. There are also echoes of previous verses: ┼Ыatakrato, which ends 27b and 28b, appears as nom. ┼Ыat├бkratuс╕е at the end of 32b. The voc. vс╣Ыtrahantama of 30a is echoed by nom. vс╣Ыtrah├бntamaс╕е in 32a and voc. vс╣Ыtrahan in the same metrical position in 33a. The end of this hymn is very tightly constructed.

With Bay Steeds to the juice we shed.

Geldner

Grassmann

Der als der Feind vertilgende sich, Indra, reich an Thaten zeigt, Mit F├╝chsen komm zu unserm Trank.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Indra bring to us the bounteous с╣Ъbhu с╣Ъbhukс╣гaс╣Зa to partake of our sacrificial viands; may he,the mighty, bring the mighty (V─Бja).тАЭ

с╣Ъbhukс╣гaс╣Зa: was the eldest and V─Бja the youngest of three brotherс╣гThe с╣Ъbhus have a share in the evening libation between Praj─Бpati and Savit─Б (Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 3.30);the с╣Ыca is addressed to the с╣Ъbhus in the evening libation on the ninth day of the dv─Бda┼Ы─Бha ceremony(Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 5.21)

Jamison Brereton

Let Indra give us the wealth belonging to craft [/R╠еbhu] as the
craftsmaster [/R╠еbhukс╣гan] for our refreshment.
Let the prizewinner give a prizewinner.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, this verse falls outside the tс╣Ыca structure and seems unconnected to the rest of the hymn. As Geldner points out, it plays on two of the names of the с╣Ъbhus, с╣Ыbh├║- itself and v─Б╠Бja-. Note also the alliteration, esp. in p─Бda b: с╣Ыbhukс╣г├бс╣Зam с╣Ыbh├║с╣Г ray├нm.

Griffith

May Indra give, to aid us, wealth handy that rules the Skilful Ones:
Yea, may the Strong give potent wealth.

Geldner

Indra soll uns zur Erlabung einen Schatz schenken, der wie Ribhuksan der erste ist, einen Ribhugeschaffenen, der Sieghafte ein sieghaftes Streitro├Я.

Grassmann

Es gebe Indra uns zum Heil, Ribhukschan, Ribhu, Vadscha uns labungsreiches Gut.
